  <div class="clearboth"></div>    </div>  </div></div>            <div id="rev-dpReviewsMostHelpful-RCKUX33F4M313" class="reviews" style="margin-top:30px;">  <div class="gry txtsmall hlp">15 of 17 people found the following review helpful</div>  <div class="clearboth"></div>  <div class="mt4 ttl"><span class="swSprite s_star_5_0 " title="5.0 out of 5 stars" ><span>5.0 out of 5 stars</span></span>   <a href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RCKUX33F4M313/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/188-0134028-9189668?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B004I8II22&nodeID=468642&store=videogames" class="txtlarge gl3 gr4 reviewTitle valignMiddle"><strong>Seem to be working fine on PS4 in a Dualshock 4</strong></a><span class="gry valignMiddle">        <span class="inlineblock txtsmall">February 3, 2014</span> </span></div>  <div class="mt4 ath"><span class="gr10">        <span class="txtsmall"><span class="gry">By</span> <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A2V4OLYNOBEP2X/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/188-0134028-9189668" class="noTextDecoration">Walt Duncan</a></span> </span>   </div>  <div class="txtsmall mt4 fvavp"><span class="inlineblock avpOrVine" ><span class="orange strong avp">Verified Purchase</span></span></div>  <div class="mt9 reviewText">       <div class="drkgry">   These are the same voltage specification as the Dualshock 4 controller, so I decided to give the 1800mAh battery a shot (DS4 comes with a 1000mAh battery).<br /><br />The battery I got looks exactly like the one in the Amazon picture, which seems to not be the case for everyone, so keep that in mind. Compared to the DS4 stock battery, this battery is taller, has the same width, but is slimmer in girth/depth; the result being that it doesn't fit in the battery tray quite the same way, but it does fit okay and doesn't move around inside the controller once reassembled. I used some tape to be sure that it would not move around. I'd suggest positioning the battery so the side closer to where you plug in the battery overhangs, because if it overhangs on the other side you can't reinstall the controller's "Reset" button.<br /><br />Turned on the controller and it seems to work fine. The controller's inbuilt speaker and rumble seem to work normally. I haven't charged it yet, but if I have anything to add to this review after I do, I will do so. Presumably I should get approximately 80% more battery life per charge than the stock battery. If the battery misses the mark by a noteworthy degree, I will adjust my review accordingly.<br /><br />I can't wholeheartedly recommend the battery to other DS4 users without more testing, but it seems great so far.<br /><br />UPDATE 1: After charging and discharging the controller once, the battery life does seem to be improved somewhere in the range of +50% to +100%. I'd say that's about what I'd hope. The recharge time doesn't seem to be very significantly longer than the time it took to recharge the original battery.<br /><br />Given my experience so far, I do recommend the battery to anyone. Perhaps some will get a lemon, but I'm satisfied with what I got for the price. </div>  </div>  <div class="imageTiles" style="margin-top:5px">   </div>  <div class="clearboth txtsmall gt9 vtStripe"> reviewTitle valignMiddle"><strong>Check the wiring before you use this battery! It could fry your controller!</strong></a><span class="gry valignMiddle">        <span class="inlineblock txtsmall">June 2, 2013</span> </span></div>  <div class="mt4 ath"><span class="gr10">        <span class="txtsmall"><span class="gry">By</span> <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/AMC0W4L616F5R/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/188-0134028-9189668" class="noTextDecoration">sgmustadio</a></span> </span>   </div>  <div class="txtsmall mt4 fvavp"><span class="inlineblock avpOrVine" ><span class="orange strong avp">Verified Purchase</span></span></div>  <div class="mt9 reviewText">       <div class="drkgry">   I bought 2 of these batteries. 1 worked great out of the box. I opened the controller and made the switch without much of a problem and it worked.<br /><br />The second battery, however, fried one of my controllers. I wish I was exaggerating - I got the magic smoke from the underside of the PCB. The controller was, needless to say, dead. I compared it to an old battery, and I noticed that the wiring to the JST connector was reversed (red and black wires were switched). This resulted in reverse voltage being applied to my controller. Apparently, PS3 controllers don't like that.<br /><br />I plan to cut and splice the wires to fix the reversed connector, but the moral here is: BE WARNED!!! Check the wires before you attach the battery! </div>  </div>  <div class="imageTiles" style="margin-top:5px">   </div>  <div class="clearboth txtsmall gt9 vtStripe">    <div class="fl cmt">     <a Benscoter</a></span> </span>   </div>  <div class="txtsmall mt4 fvavp"><span class="inlineblock avpOrVine" ><span class="orange strong avp">Verified Purchase</span></span></div>  <div class="mt9 reviewText">       <div class="drkgry">   I questioned purchasing this because I thought there had to be no way this battery was any good. I am very glad I went ahead with the purchase. This has resolved my battery issues with my PS3 controller. I've had it for a few months and am still happy with the longevity of the charge.<br /><br />My only suggestion is to be very careful when replacing it. Although I knew better I did not replace the battery over a flat surface and rushed the process a bit. It still went off without a hitch, but one of the springs for a trigger button is not on perfectly now so it doesn't spring back as quickly as it did before. This of course it operator error.
